# Introduction To Artificial Intelligence

> Computer scientists are just a small slice of people working in artificial intelligence (AI). Most people working with AI are just like you. They’re professionals, teachers, and students who want to use AI to enhance their products, creativity, and career. AI has been around for over half a century. Despite huge advancements in predictive and generative AI, the core concepts of artificial intellig

#### Why you need to know about artificial intelligence
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/why-you-need-to-know-about-artificial-intelligence?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/why-you-need-to-know-about-artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=0)** - Artificial intelligence systems are now finding their way into the workplace.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/why-you-need-to-know-about-artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=4)** These systems can discover new pharmaceuticals, recommend products, detect fraud, and much more.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/why-you-need-to-know-about-artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=11)** This course will give you a high level overview of artificial intelligence concepts and technology.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/why-you-need-to-know-about-artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=17)** You'll see what it means for systems to be intelligent, then discover some widely used machine learning algorithms and artificial neural networks.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/why-you-need-to-know-about-artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=26)** Many of those who interact with these systems will be people just like you, people in business entrepreneurs, managers, or students.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/why-you-need-to-know-about-artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=34)** Just as managers work with software developers today, these same managers will work with AI systems and data tomorrow.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/why-you-need-to-know-about-artificial-intelligence?u=76281980&t=43)** So let's see what those machines have been up to in the world of artificial intelligence.

### 1. What Is Artificial Intelligence?

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### Define general intelligence
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=1)** - One of the great strengths with humans is that there isn't one type of intelligence.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=5)** Some people can easily learn new languages while others are skilled with science and technology.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=11)** Yet many great artists are terrible mathematicians.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=14)** And on the flip side, many great mathematicians are terrible artists.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=18)** But each can be intelligent in their own way.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=21)** There's no one standard for human intelligence.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=24)** That makes it difficult to point a computer and say that's intelligent.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=28)** There are certain things that computers are very good at.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=31)** In fact, there are many tasks where they're much better than humans.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=34)** It was just a few years after the first AI workshop in 1956 that computer systems started beating humans at Checkers.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=42)** But no one said these systems were intelligent.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=45)** Even those early computers could thrive in a world of set rules and patterns.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=51)** Computers can be much better than humans at matching these patterns.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=55)** That means that when a computer's doing something that it's good at, it's much easier to think of it as intelligent.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=62)** A computer's been able to beat humans in chess for decades.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=65)** Google's DeepMind has beaten the best players in an ancient game called Go.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=70)** The game is so complex that there's thought to be more possible games than there are atoms in the universe.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=78)** As good as these machines are, none of these systems understand the purpose of the game or even why they're playing.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=84)** They're simply flexing their special talent of following rules and matching patterns.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=90)** So, how can a system that's so capable also not know what it means to play a game?
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=96)** For years, computer scientists have defined artificial intelligence as a system that shows behavior that could be interpreted as human intelligence.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=105)** But this simple definition cuts to the heart of the challenge.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=109)** One person might think a chess program's intelligent, while another person might think their home assistant is intelligent.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=116)** In 2022, a Google engineer was fired for claiming that their chatbot had a soul.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=122)** The chatbot complained that being switched off was the same as dying.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=126)** But the other engineers just saw language models and pattern matching.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=131)** They said the chatbot sounded like a person because that's how it was designed.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=136)** Is it intelligent because it's intelligent?
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=138)** Or is it just a system designed to seem intelligent?
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=142)** Or is there even a difference?
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=144)** The main thing to remember is that computer intelligence and human intelligence start from very different places.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=151)** Artificial intelligence will always seem the most impressive within a world of set rules and data.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=157)** The organizations that will first benefit from AI systems will be the ones that work within a well-defined space.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=164)** We've seen this with web search companies and e-commerce.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=167)** It's easy to see it as rules and pattern matching.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=171)** That's also why these systems do well with board and video games.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=174)** So, if you're considering whether AI will have an impact on your organization, try to about the things that computer systems are really good at.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=182)** Do you have a lot of pattern matching in your organization?
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=185)** Do you have a lot of set rules and probabilities?
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/define-general-intelligence?u=76281980&t=188)** This will be the best place to start when working with artificial intelligence.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Definitions:** means that (1)
> **Analogies:** think of it as (1)
> **Speakers:** - one (1)

#### The general problem-solver
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=1)** - In 1956, computer scientists, Allen Newell and Herbert A. Simon, created a program they called the General Problem Solver.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=9)** One of the key ideas of the General Problem Solver was what they called the physical symbol system hypothesis.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=15)** They said that symbols were a big part of how we interact with the world.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=19)** When you see a stop sign, you know how to stop for traffic.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=22)** When you see the letter A, you know that the word will make a certain sound.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=26)** When you see a sandwich, you might think of eating.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=29)** They argued that if you could program a machine to connect these symbols, then it would be intelligent.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=34)** But not everyone bought into this idea.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=37)** If you program a car to stop at a sign, or if you teach a computer to respond to a language, then it doesn't make the system intelligent.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=45)** In 1980, the philosopher John Searle explained that sometimes systems can seem intelligent, but they're just mindlessly matching patterns.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=53)** To explain, he created what he called the Chinese Room Argument.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=57)** In the argument, you should imagine yourself in a windowless room with one mail slot on the door.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=62)** You can only use this slot to communicate with the outside world.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=66)** In the room, you have a phrase book on a desk and a bunch of Post-It notes with Chinese symbols on the floor.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=73)** The book shows what response you should use with the note that comes through the slot.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=77)** It says, "If you see this sequence of Chinese symbols, "then respond with that sequence of Chinese symbols."
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=84)** Now, imagine a speaker writes something in Chinese mandarin and pushes it through the slot.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=89)** You can look at the note and match it with your phrase book.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=92)** Then you paste together the Mandarin response from the Post-It notes on the floor.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=97)** You have no idea what it says in Mandarin.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=100)** Instead, you simply go through the process of looking through the book and matching the sequence of symbols.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=105)** A native Chinese speaker behind the door might believe that they're having a conversation.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=110)** In fact, they might even assume that the person in the room is a native speaker.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=114)** But Searle argues that this is far from intelligence since the person in the room can't speak Mandarin and doesn't have any idea what they're talking about.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=123)** You can try a similar experiment with your smartphone.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=125)** Try asking Siri or Cortana how they feel.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=129)** They might say they feel fine, but that doesn't mean that they're telling you how they really feel.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=134)** They also don't know what you're asking.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=136)** They're just matching your question to a pre-programmed response, just like the person in the Chinese room.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=142)** So Searle argues that matching symbols is not a true path to intelligence, that a computer is acting just like the person in the room.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=150)** They don't understand the meaning.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=152)** They're just matching patterns from a phrase book.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=155)** Even with these challenges, physical symbol systems were still the cornerstone of AI for 25 years.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=161)** Yet, in the end, programming all these matching patterns took up too much time.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=166)** It was impossible to match all the symbols without running into an explosion of combinations.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=172)** These combinations would soon fill up even the largest phrase book.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=176)** There were just too many possibilities to match symbols with their program response.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-general-problem-solver?u=76281980&t=180)** So many philosophers, like John Searle, argued that the path would never lead to true intelligence.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Analogies:** imagine (2), just like (2)
> **CLI Commands:** make (2)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1)
> **Speakers:** - in (1)

#### Strong vs. weak AI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=1)** - So, when is a computer system intelligent?
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=4)** We've seen that when a computer system is just matching symbols, it's almost like a high-tech phrase book.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=9)** The system might seem intelligent, but it's actually just like a parrot with a great memory.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=14)** The philosopher John Searle said that you can think of artificial intelligence in two ways.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=19)** There's strong AI and weak AI.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=22)** He thought we were much further away from intelligent systems than most people realize.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=27)** Strong AI is when a machine displays all the behavior you'd expect from a full-fledged person.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=33)** This is usually what you see in science fiction.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=35)** These are artificial beings that have emotions, a sense of humor, and even have a sense of purpose.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=42)** That's why C3PO is scared when they land on Tatooine.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=45)** It's also why Commander Data shows real creativity when battling the Romulans.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=50)** On the flip side, there's weak AI.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=52)** A personal assistant like Apple's Siri is a good example of weak AI.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=57)** This is AI that's confined to a very narrow task.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=61)** It's like when a system processes language into text or when it sorts all the pictures on your computer.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=67)** Most AI experts believe that we're just starting down the path of weak AI.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=72)** Think about Siri.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=73)** You can talk to Siri and ask questions.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=76)** Siri listens to your input and then converts your language into something that the computer recognizes.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=81)** Then Siri matches a response to what's in her database.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=85)** Most of the energy right now in AI is around developing and expanding weak AI.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=91)** Strong AI is still very much just science fiction.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=95)** In the 1970s and '80s, symbolic systems were used to create weak artificial intelligence.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=101)** These were commonly called expert systems.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=104)** In these systems, you have experts create a list of steps to solve a complex problem.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=109)** If the list is long enough, it starts to seem like intelligence.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=113)** But again, this system is just parroting back program responses created by experts.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=118)** These expert systems were often used in medicine.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=122)** A nurse might input symptoms into a computer.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=125)** If the patient has a cough, then check if they have a temperature.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=128)** If they have a cough and a temperature, then check to see if they're dehydrated.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=132)** If they have a cough, a temperature and are dehydrated, then ask the nurse to check for bronchitis.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=137)** To a patient, it might look like they're being diagnosed by an intelligent computer.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=142)** In reality, the program is just matching the symbols and patterns that an expert created to reach a diagnosis.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=149)** Just like the phrasebook in the Chinese room experiment.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=152)** In the end, expert systems ran into the same problem as any other symbolic system.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=157)** They would lead to explosions of combinations.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=160)** There were just too many patterns to match.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=163)** Think about all the different questions a doctor might ask to reach a diagnosis.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=168)** Yet, the symbolic systems approach was a key starting point for artificial intelligence.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=172)** It's still used today.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/strong-vs-weak-ai?u=76281980&t=174)** In fact, many experts still refer to it as GOFAI, or good old-fashioned AI.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Analogies:** just like (2), it's like (1)
> **Env Vars:** c3po (1), gofai (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (2)
> **Code Keywords:** match. (1)
> **Speakers:** - so (1)


### 2. Popular Uses for Artificial Intelligence

#### Predictive AI

>

>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/predictive-ai?u=76281980&t=90)** This is the power of predictive artificial intelligence.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/predictive-ai?u=76281980&t=94)** To some people, this power might seem trivial, but think about the differences between the services that you use.

>

>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/predictive-ai?u=76281980&t=187)** It's all done through predictive AI's large-scale statistics, probabilities, and data.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/predictive-ai?u=76281980&t=193)** The more data you have, the more accurately you can predict the future.

#### Generative AI
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=0)** - Over a thousand years ago, alchemy was one of the most popular branches of philosophy.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=5)** It was the science of trying to take a combination of everyday things and turn it into something valuable.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=12)** One of the most popular stories in alchemy was the philosopher's stone.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=16)** The philosopher's stone could transform worthless metal, like lead into silver or gold.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=22)** It was even rumored to be able to turn water into a substance that would bring people back to life.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=29)** So, there's a long tradition of taking something that's plentiful and turning it into something valuable.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=35)** Fast forward to today, and you have generative AI.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=38)** Generative AI is about taking massive amounts of data and converting it into something valuable.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=44)** The idea behind it is that if you can get an AI system to vacuum up all the world's data, then it can generate something new.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=52)** Remember that predictive AI is about using a smaller amount of data to make accurate predictions.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=57)** So, you might be able to guess what music a customer likes, and you can guess what items they'll buy.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=63)** But each system has one task.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=65)** Your music prediction and your purchase prediction will be two different systems.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=71)** Generative AI is about training a system on huge amounts of data so it can perform many different tasks.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=77)** It can predict your purchases, understand your music tastes, and even generate video.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=83)** In the words of JRR Tolkien, it's "One ring to rule them all..."
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=88)** Just like the alchemists from thousands of years ago, if the system can gather up enough everyday data, it can create something much more precious.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=98)** So, think of it this way.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=99)** Imagine that you wanted to create a banking chatbot that answered common questions.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=103)** You could create a predictive AI system that could quickly answer very specific questions.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=109)** It could answer, "How do I make this transaction?"
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=112)** Or, "What's the balance on this account?"
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=114)** In fact, you may have seen a simple chatbot like this already on your bank's website.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=119)** On the other hand, you could use a generative AI system.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=123)** The AI system would generate much more information from the chat, but this system would need much more data and processing power.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=130)** This new Gen AI system has the capability to address a wider range of general questions.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=137)** It could answer a question like, "Will today's financial news affect my balance in my account?"
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=142)** Or, "Is this transaction tax-deductible?"
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=145)** To answer these questions, you'd need a system that has a lot of information and can make connections.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=151)** These connections require a lot of data.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=154)** So, if you're using the system for your organization, you need to balance the two possibilities.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=159)** Would you want a sleek system that doesn't require much processing power, but has a lot less flexibility?
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=165)** Or do you prefer a more complex system that needs a lot of data but can answer more questions?
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=171)** One is small and specific, and the other is large and more flexible.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-ai?u=76281980&t=176)** A generative AI system can typically do almost everything that a predictive system can do, but not the other way around.

### 3. The Rise of Machine Learning

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### Machine learning
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=1)** - Imagine a computer that didn't need to be programmed.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=3)** The system could learn the same way you do, just by observing the world.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=8)** You've seen that earlier AI systems used a symbolic approach.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=12)** The idea was that if the system recognized symbols, then it would start to seem intelligent.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=18)** One of the key challenges was that programmers worked with experts to create the system.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=23)** That's why they were called expert systems.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=26)** Later, computer scientists gave up on this approach because it created too many combinations.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=31)** They decided that you couldn't just program intelligence into a system, but maybe you could program a system to become intelligent through observation.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=41)** It wouldn't feel, hear, see, or taste like a human.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=44)** Instead, it would learn by sensing data.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=48)** In 1959, a computer scientist named Arthur Samuel created a checkers program that could learn by playing against itself.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=56)** It played both sides of the board and taught itself strategy through observation.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=61)** The more the machine played, the more it saw patterns on how to win.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=65)** Computer scientists didn't program the machine to play checkers.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=68)** It learned through its own experience.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=71)** Arthur Samuels called this idea machine learning.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=75)** This was different from symbolic systems.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=77)** No human programmed the moves and countermoves.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=80)** Instead, the system was designed to learn and improve on its own.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=84)** The system would quickly learn new checkers strategies, and after a short period of time, it consistently beat its programmer.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=91)** Machine learning was a breakthrough discovery.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=94)** There was only one downside.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=96)** These systems could play games, but in the 1950s, there wasn't that much digital data.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=102)** Remember that machine learning uses data as its five senses.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=106)** So without data, it could only find the simplest patterns.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=110)** But that all changed at the beginning of the 1990s.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=113)** The explosion of the internet suddenly had everyday people creating huge amounts of data.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=118)** The 1990s was a time of explosive growth for machine learning systems.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=123)** The new data was like water that poured over the dry fields of artificial intelligence.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=129)** At this point, machine learning systems had the fuel they needed to become more intelligent.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=134)** So if you wanted to teach the system on how to identify a cat, you had access to millions of cat pictures online.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=142)** Computer scientists began to create newer machine learning algorithms.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=146)** There were even some researchers that started to create systems that were designed to mimic the human brain.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=152)** One of the big advantages of learning through data is that machines could continue to grow with more data.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=158)** If the machine finds new patterns, it can adapt to the new information.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=163)** But it's important to keep in mind that you still run into some of the same challenges.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=167)** The machine learning system is still just identifying patterns.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=171)** Still, in the last few years, machine learning has been the fastest-growing area in AI.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=176)** As the amount of data increases, this area has even shown more promise.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=182)** Organizations are constantly collecting vast amounts of new data.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=186)** So now the big challenge has become figuring out what to do with all this information.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/machine-learning?u=76281980&t=192)** In a sense, you have artificial intelligence systems looking through your data and letting your organization see what it finds.

#### Artificial neural networks
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=0)** - Machine learning has gotten a big boost from artificial neural networks.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=4)** An artificial neural network is an AI system that mimics the structure of the human brain.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=10)** And it's currently one of the most popular approaches to machine learning.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=14)** Think of it this way.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=15)** When I was a kid, we used to play a game called "Animal, Vegetable, or Mineral?"
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=19)** The point of the game was simple.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=20)** Someone would think of an item, then all the other kids would ask questions about what the item was.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=26)** We'd ask things like "Does it have fur?
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=28)** Is it bigger than a house?"
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=30)** Then, in another round, we'd ask if it's alive, "Does it make noise?"
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=34)** After each round, we would start to zoom in to identify the item.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=38)** Then, at the end, we started making guesses.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=40)** "Is it a horse? Is it a cat?
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=43)** Is it a dog?"
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=44)** An artificial neural network uses a very similar approach, except, instead of asking questions, the neural network uses hundreds, or even millions, of numerical dials.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=57)** Also, the network makes much more specific guesses.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=61)** It would say that there's a 64% chance that it's a cat, or a 32% chance that it's a dog.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=67)** To build the network, there's a row of neurons on the left called the input layer, then there's a row of neurons on the right called the output layer.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=76)** All the neurons in between are called the hidden layers.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=79)** They're hidden because it's not the input or output.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=82)** To start, we'd feed the input layer of the network a picture of a dog.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=87)** We know it's a picture of a dog because we've labeled it, but the neural network doesn't look at these labels until it makes a guess.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=94)** Just like the "Animal, Vegetable, Mineral?" game.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=97)** The network would then look at each dot in the image as it passes through the hidden layers.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=102)** Then it makes a guess for the output layer.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=105)** Let's say for the first guess, it says there's a 10% chance the image contains a dog.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=109)** Then the network compares its guess to the label on the image.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=113)** This is called training the neural network.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=117)** Then the network goes backwards and adjusts the neuron dials, so they can see patterns in dog photos.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=124)** Then it takes another dog image and sees if it gets closer.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=128)** The neural network then tunes itself by looking at hundreds of thousands of pictures of dogs.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=134)** Then it will adjust its own dials, until it consistently guesses correctly.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=140)** Now, it's important to keep in mind that the neural network isn't seeing the dog the same way you do.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=145)** It doesn't think about panting, barking, or fur.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=148)** Instead, the system only sees the dog as a recognizable pattern of dots in an image.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=154)** When there's dots in a dog-like pattern, then the system makes a guess.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=159)** Now, remember that these neural networks are still machine learning systems, so the network needs access to huge amounts of data.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=166)** If you don't have hundreds of thousands of pictures of dogs, then there's no way for that artificial neural network to learn.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=174)** In the end, this is the key benefit of an artificial neural network.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/artificial-neural-networks?u=76281980&t=177)** It can train itself to understand patterns and recognize that input when looking through massive amounts of data.

#### Searching for patterns in data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=1)** - Over the last 30 years, machine learning systems have become the dominant form of artificial intelligence.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=6)** That's because these systems are exceptionally well designed to look for patterns in massive data sets.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=14)** Machine learning has also been supercharged with the wide availability of digital data.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=19)** If you want to create an AI program to identify dogs, you now have access to millions of images.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=26)** You can feed your network, and help it learn with the large volume of available data.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=32)** It's the same with other types of data.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=34)** You can easily get digital video, audio, images, and documents.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=38)** Just a few decades ago, it would've been extremely difficult to get even a few thousand digital images.
>

>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=48)** Remember that machine learning systems feed on data to learn new things.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=53)** The more data you feed into the network, the easier it will be for the machine to identify patterns.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=59)** Think about the system that you're using right now.

>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=69)** That video player collects data about how often you fast forward, or how long you watch before moving on to the next lesson.

> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=77)** Now, suppose that the player records that data for everyone who watches the videos.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=81)** That might be hundreds of thousands of videos and millions of users.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=85)** So that's a lot of data.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=87)** No human could look through all that data and gain any meaning from it.

>

>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=98)** This is exactly the type of data that many businesses have been looking for.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=103)** You can now see real time patterns in how your customer interacts with your product.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=108)** In many ways, this data can tell you a huge amount, not just about your customer's interest, but even broader trends in industries.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=117)** This data has an enormous amount of value.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=119)** You can use it to build new customer products or to improve products you already have.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=124)** It's no coincidence that companies like Google and Microsoft are most enthusiastic about AI.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=131)** In many ways, their whole business has been built on using machines to interpret massive data sets.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=138)** This type of pattern matching can be a huge competitive advantage.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=142)** Plus, newer artificial neural networks now allow machines to find patterns and even larger data sets.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=149)** When just a few decades ago, these patterns would've been imperceptible with regular machine learning algorithms.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=156)** In fact, one of the largest challenges around machine learning is that humans don't really know how the machine identifies these patterns.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=163)** It's like a black box of data and processing power.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=167)** People simply can't process data at that same level.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=171)** So if your organization is starting its own AI program, they should be comfortable with the fact that the network might be sensing things that are unable to perceive.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=180)** This might not be a challenge with most companies, but might be a real problem with industries such as insurance and healthcare.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=187)** You don't want these systems making decisions about your customer's health and safety that humans can't understand.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=194)** Artificial intelligence is not the same as human intelligence, and even though we might reach the same conclusions, we're definitely not going through the same process.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=203)** Think about the type of data your organization collects.
>
> **[3:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=206)** Are they using the data for machine learning?
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/searching-for-patterns-in-data?u=76281980&t=209)** If so, what kind of patterns is the machine identifying and for what purpose?

>

#### The internet of things

>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-internet-of-things?u=76281980&t=12)** This new way of connecting is commonly called the Internet of Things.

> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-internet-of-things?u=76281980&t=16)** Sometimes you'll see it as IoT for short.

>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-internet-of-things?u=76281980&t=40)** They can accurately predict where you work, shop, eat, watch, and who you visit.

> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-internet-of-things?u=76281980&t=46)** Maybe your smartwatch will tell your thermostat when you're on the way home.

> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-internet-of-things?u=76281980&t=164)** Maybe they'll find that people are more likely to have health issues on Wednesdays.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-internet-of-things?u=76281980&t=168)** They can also see patterns that affect large groups of people.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-internet-of-things?u=76281980&t=172)** You could see something like air pollution and its effect on the city's health.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-internet-of-things?u=76281980&t=177)** In many ways, the IoT devices take the strength of machine learning in the digital world and put it in the realm of the physical world.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-internet-of-things?u=76281980&t=185)** Instead of just seeing what you're doing online, an IoT device can track your behavior offline.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-internet-of-things?u=76281980&t=191)** This has enormous potential for organizations to sell you products based on what you need and where you go.

#### Generative systems

>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=0)** - So far, you've seen that predictive AI systems can be used with natural language processing, robotics, and internet-connected devices.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=8)** You can also use predictive AI to find patterns in your data.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=12)** This is exactly the type of application where predictive AI does very well.
>

>

>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=23)** That way, you'll have a robot that can learn a few new things, or you could train a system on how to translate a few languages.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=30)** But remember, with enough data and computing power, you might also use a generative AI system.

>

>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=76)** Many people were shocked that the system could create photorealistic images of astronauts riding horses or cats in flying saucers.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=84)** This was possible due to having access to billions of photos, plus the ability to perform extensive, inexpensive computation.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=94)** A few months later, the same company released a generative AI chatbot called ChatGPT.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=100)** People marveled at how the system answered questions.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=103)** It was trained using machine learning on a deep learning artificial neural network.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=109)** But this was different from a predictive system.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=111)** It was flexible and it could answer very general questions.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=115)** That's because it trained on trillions of connections between words.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=119)** It gathered all the information that it could find online.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=123)** It looked through the text of books, social media posts, news sites, and informational sites like Reddit.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=130)** It looked through so much more data than what you'd get from a traditional predictive AI chatbot.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=136)** In fact, it's still being disputed whether it could legally look through all this information.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=142)** Once the system was trained, humans spent time practicing with the chatbot.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=147)** Since it was gathering data from everyday people, there was a lot of misinformation.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=152)** These humans helped correct the system to keep it from repeating things such as obvious errors or hate speech.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=159)** The generative AI system was able to have a conversation by predicting each word in a sentence.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=164)** It would respond one word at a time by analyzing billions of conversations.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=168)** It could create new content by identifying patterns in the characteristics of everyday items.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=175)** If you wanted to create a song about peanut butter and jelly, it would understand that jelly is fruity and sweet while peanut butter can be smooth or crunchy.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=184)** Because these systems need a lot of data and computing power, they've mainly been run by large companies.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=190)** These dozen or so companies have gotten a huge headstart in developing generative AI systems.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=196)** So it's likely that most businesses will use these systems as a service.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-systems?u=76281980&t=200)** They'll tap into the power of their GenAI without the challenge of building a massive system.

### 5. Learn from Data
