#### Large language models (LLM)
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=0)** - Imagine if everywhere you went there were parrots, they would stare at you and listen.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=6)** They would read your email and look at your credit card transactions.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=9)** They remember every word that you said and read everything that you wrote, and then they would just repeat back what they heard.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=17)** It almost sounds like a creepy old Alfred Hitchcock movie.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=21)** On top of that, these parrots aren't just interested in you, they're interested in everyone, and they're everywhere.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=28)** They're in every room, car, gym, subway, hotel, and airplane.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=34)** Now, imagine that these parrots are working together.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=37)** That means that a parrot that listens to you at the gym will know all the same information as the parrot that lives in your living room.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=45)** Think about all the data these parrots would have.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=48)** The billions of times that they've heard someone say, "Have a nice day", or the billions of questions that they've heard answered.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=54)** Over time this creepy network of parrots would start to seem extremely intelligent, but remember, they're just parrots.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=63)** They're just repeating back to you what they've heard.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=66)** It might sound strange, but this is very similar to how a gen AI large language model works.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=73)** These models look through billions of sentences and trillions of words.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=77)** They vacuum up email conversations and credit card receipts.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=81)** Then they use that information to parrot back answers to almost any question.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=87)** That's why linguistic expert Emily Bender refers to this type of foundation model as stochastic parrots.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=94)** They argue that large language models don't understand the meaning of what they're saying.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=99)** Instead, these models just parrot back phrases one word at a time based on probabilities and guesswork.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=106)** In many ways, this is like the Chinese room argument that you saw earlier.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=110)** Remember that philosopher John Searle argued that machine learning systems could never reach true intelligence?
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=117)** That at best these systems could just repeat back responses based on a phrase book.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=123)** Professor Bender takes this argument a step further.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=126)** She says that not only can these systems never achieve intelligence, but that their fake intelligence can also be dangerous.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=134)** You saw earlier that these large language models will often hallucinate.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=138)** That means that the chat system will easily mix facts and fiction.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=143)** These systems can suggest strange health advice like eating rocks or provide false information about historical figures.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=151)** Bender and others argue that this is a symptom of how these systems operate, that it's not that LLMs are ignorant of facts, but it's just they just don't care if it's a fact.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=162)** They argue that this is a bug that can be fixed.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=165)** Instead, it's an expected side effect of learning without understanding any meaning.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=171)** Others argue that as foundation models process more data, they'll gain a better understanding of the facts, that they'll do a better job separating out facts from fiction.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=180)** If John Searle and Emily Bender are right, then these systems will never truly understand the meaning behind what they're saying.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=187)** They'll just be parrots that make it seem like you're having a conversation, but they'll just be repeating a remix of billions of other conversations.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=196)** It's also important to keep in mind that an AI chat bot like ChatGPT doesn't really need to understand the meaning to help you write a better email message.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=207)** That's why it's important to keep in mind that there's a big difference between being intelligent and seeming intelligent.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/large-language-models-llm?u=76281980&t=213)** Gen AI chat bots can certainly act like they're intelligent, and for most people, that's more than enough.

> **Analogies:** imagine (2), similar to (1)

#### Image diffusion models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=0)** - Imagine that you are in a bakery standing in front of six beautiful cakes.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=4)** Two were chocolate, the other two were vanilla, one looked like a wedding cake, and another was a Brazilian brigadeiro.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=12)** As you stand there, someone tells you that you're the new baker.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=15)** You've never baked in your life, but you grab a bowl and start baking.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=19)** How would you teach yourself how to bake cakes?
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=22)** Imagine that there's no recipes and no other chefs.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=25)** You just need to figure out how to bake a cake on your own.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=29)** This is a lot like the challenge that generative AI systems run into when creating new images.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=35)** The system didn't get to see the people, ingredients, or techniques that went into making the images.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=40)** In a sense, the images are baked cakes.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=44)** To generate a new image, the system needs to teach itself how to un-bake, and then re-bake, billions of images.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=52)** So to do this, you put on an apron and smash each one of the cakes into mounds of mush.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=60)** Now you have six mounds of chocolate, vanilla, eggs, cream, butter, and sugar.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=65)** Each of them mashed up into a multicolored mess.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=70)** And now your job is to re-bake these mounds back into the same neatly designed cakes.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=77)** Ideally, someone should be able to walk into the bakery and never know that they've been mushed and re-baked.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=84)** That might sound strange, but that's very similar to how image diffusion models work with generative AI systems.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=91)** To learn how to generate new images the system blurs, or diffuses, each image until it's destroyed.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=99)** You end up with a cloudy, colorful graphic like a mushed up cake.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=104)** Then the system sharpens the images until they match the original.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=109)** Ideally, they should look exactly the same.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=112)** So why would the Gen AI system go through this terrible process of destroying and then recreating images?
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=118)** Remember, the generative AI systems create something new.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=122)** There's no guidebook for generating new images.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=125)** There's no one set of rules to create an image of an astronaut standing on a brick wall.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=131)** The system needs to know all the lines and colors that went into a brick wall.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=135)** Then it needs to know all the different patterns that make up images of astronauts.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=139)** Then it needs to put the two together.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=142)** It has to be complete with shadows and a realistic perspective.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=146)** You could only get that kind of knowledge by having a deep understanding of the ingredients.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=152)** It's like someone going into the bakery and asking for a half chocolate, half vanilla wedding cake.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=159)** You know all the ingredients because you've baked and destroyed many different versions of similar cakes.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=165)** It's only by fully understanding the ingredients that you could generate something new.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=171)** Now image diffusion models, like all foundation models, rely on an enormous amount of data.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=177)** If the system wants to generate something new, it's going to have to rely on a lot more than just six cakes.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=184)** These models will look through billions of images and identify patterns using statistics.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=190)** It won't see a cake or a wall or an astronaut the same way that you do.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=195)** Instead it will see pixelated patterns that it's learned through self-supervised learning.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=201)** It destroyed and recreated all those images.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/image-diffusion-models?u=76281980&t=205)** It's through this terrible process of destruction and recreation that these generative AI systems learn how to create something new.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** new. (3), this, (1), new, (1), self (1)
> **Analogies:** imagine (2), it's like (1)
> **CLI Commands:** make (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1)
> **Speakers:** - imagine (1)


### 12. Generative AI Architecture

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### Generative adversarial networks (GAN)
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=0)** - Self supervised foundation models, like diffusion models, have been one of the most successful ways to generate new images.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=7)** It's a foundation model, so these systems need a lot of data, but have a lot of flexibility.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=12)** But sometimes people just want a more common image.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=15)** They just want the system to generate a portrait or a mountain range.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=18)** They don't need a mouse wearing a hat or an astronaut standing on a brick wall.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=23)** If you're okay giving up some flexibility, then there are other ways to generate photorealistic images.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=30)** One of the most popular is creating a generative adversarial network, or GAN.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=36)** These GANs don't use self supervised learning or a foundation model.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=41)** In fact, you could get by with just regular, old unsupervised and supervised learning.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=46)** The key to thinking about GANs is to focus on the word adversarial.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=51)** It's like putting two artificial neural networks in a boxing ring and having them fight it out.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=56)** One neural network is called the generator.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=59)** This system uses unsupervised learning to generate new images.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=63)** Its first attempts will look like splashing paint on the wall.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=67)** The second neural network is called the discriminator.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=70)** This system uses a form of supervised learning that classifies photos.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=74)** It'll look at an image and determine whether it's real or a fake photograph.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=79)** So imagine that you created this adversarial network to create a professional looking portrait.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=84)** The generator might start by just splashing color, then will forward that splashed image to the discriminator.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=91)** The discriminator will quickly recognize that this is not a real photograph.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=95)** It will reject the image and have the generator try again.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=99)** Then the generator will tweak the image based on the discriminator's feedback.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=103)** Maybe it will splash color in the form of a circle as an attempt to generate a face.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=108)** Again, the discriminator will reject the image and give the generator feedback.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=113)** The discriminator and the generator will be locked in this battle.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=117)** The generator tries to trick the discriminator, and the discriminator tries to classify real photographs.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=123)** After billions of failed attempts, the generator will start producing photorealistic images.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=130)** The discriminator will start having a difficult time figuring out if the image is a real photograph.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=137)** At some point, the generator will create an image that the discriminator won't be able to classify as fake, and by that time, there's a good chance you won't be able to tell either.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=148)** Generative adversarial networks can produce extremely photorealistic images, but there are a couple of downsides compared to diffusion models.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=157)** The first is that the discriminator only classifies photographs where it's been trained.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=162)** So if the discriminator is only trained on human portraits, the system can only generate these portraits.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=169)** Plus, as you've already seen, you can't really use this system to generate compositions.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=174)** You can't create images of dolphins in spacesuits.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=177)** It can only generate images trained on existing photos.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=182)** The upside to these systems is that they don't rely on a foundation model, so they need much less data, and are easier to set up.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=191)** That's why generative adversarial networks are great for creating an AI system that can produce realistic looking photographs.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/generative-adversarial-networks-gan?u=76281980&t=199)** You can generate fake human portraits or landscape photos, while diffusion models work better if you want to generate something completely new.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** self (2), new. (1)
> **Definitions:** is called (2), is a  (1)
> **Analogies:** it's like (1), imagine (1)
> **Env Vars:** gan (1)
> **Prerequisites:** set up (1)
> **Speakers:** - self (1)

#### Variational autoencoder (VAE)
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=0)** - Generative artificial intelligence and foundation models can give you an enormous amount of flexibility, but you've already seen that sometimes you don't need all that power.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=9)** This is particularly true if you want to colorize an old image or increase its resolution.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=15)** For that, you might want to try an autoencoder.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=19)** Autoencoders are the silent work engine from many of the AI image tools that you'll use today.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=25)** They'll use supervised or unsupervised machine learning to come up with a pattern of perfection.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=31)** They can be trained with supervised or unsupervised learning to look through millions of images of similar subjects.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=38)** Then the autoencoder will encode all these images into perfect versions of the subject.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=45)** So if your photograph contains a vase, then the system will have encoded the essence of the vase.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=51)** Then this essence of tens of thousands of vases can improve the picture of your imperfect vase.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=59)** In a sense, they try to encode the essence of an image and then decode any new images to match this pattern of perfection.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=69)** So say you have an image of a tree that's from an old photograph, autoencoders can make it look like a modern photograph by sharpening and even colorizing the image.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=79)** The most popular autoencoder is the variational autoencoder.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=84)** These encoders can look for patterns and images, let's say tree images.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=90)** Then it will cluster together the essence of these tree images.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=94)** This process is called encoding.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=96)** It extracts the tree from a latent space.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=100)** You can almost imagine it like a pencil outline of a tree.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=104)** Then the artificial neural network can use this pencil outline or code to enhance or even generate new tree images.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=113)** That means that the encoder will be able to separate the tree from the old scratches or grainy noise.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=119)** Then it can remove that noise and produce a much clear image of a tree.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=124)** In a sense, the system is separating out the signal, which is the tree, from the noise, which is all the parts of the image that are not the tree.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=134)** For a variational autoencoder, all the non-tree items in the image are called anomalies.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=141)** That's why part of the encoding is called anomaly detection.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=145)** You're detecting the parts of the photo that are not the tree, and then filtering them out.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=151)** Once you have that pure tree code, you can use the system to decode the image as a perfect copy or create one that's been dramatically improved.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=162)** Now, autoencoders do suffer from some of the challenges of traditional predictive AI.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=166)** These systems can only create perfect trees or vases if it's already been trained on thousands or even tens of thousands of labeled images.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=176)** Plus, it doesn't have the flexibility you get from a foundation model.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=181)** You wouldn't be able to generate a vase with a tree inside.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=185)** But for bread-and-butter image enhancement, autoencoders are a very powerful way to improve your images.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=191)** It's always fun to generate new images, but many photographers, artists and graphic designers are just looking to enhance the images they already have.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/variational-autoencoder-vae?u=76281980&t=201)** So even though this technique is a form of predictive AI, it's still plenty useful for anyone who works with digital images.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Definitions:** is called (2), means that (1), is a  (1)
> **Analogies:** picture (1), imagine (1)
> **CLI Commands:** make (1)
> **Code Keywords:** let (1)
> **Speakers:** - generative (1)

#### Transformers
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=0)** - In 2017, researchers at Google and the University of Toronto came up with a paper called "Attention is All You Need."
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=8)** This paper was trying to come up with a new way to translate English into French and German.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=14)** There are a lot of sentences where a simple change in word order can dramatically change the meaning.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=19)** Think about these two sentences.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=21)** I want to paint the wall blue.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=23)** I want to paint the blue wall.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=26)** In the first sentence, you have no idea what color the wall is you want to paint.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=31)** It could be black, brown, or even unpainted.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=34)** In the second sentence, you know the color of the wall, but you have no idea what color to paint the wall.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=40)** That means that when you translate these two sentences, you need to really understand the differences between the two meanings.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=47)** To solve this problem, these researchers proposed a transformer model.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=52)** This model is like the autoencoders that you saw earlier.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=56)** Remember that autoencoders find the essence of the item in the photograph.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=60)** You could almost think of it like a pencil drawing.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=63)** The system encodes the tree and then uses that code to decode images of other trees.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=70)** A transformer uses a similar technique to encode large blocks of text, except here, the system is trying to find the purpose of the sentence instead of the essence of the image.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=84)** It does this by assigning a numerical value to how each word is ordered in the sentence.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=90)** Then over time, the system can start to learn the relationship between the purpose and when the word appears in a sentence.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=99)** Now, when the researchers came up with this model back in 2017, they were focused on language translation, but it turns out that transformers were one of the best ways to understand the purpose behind language.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=112)** That's why in 2019, companies such as Google and OpenAI started to create transformer-based chat systems.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=121)** Remember that ChatGPT stands for generative pre-trained transformer.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=128)** One key thing to remember is that transformer-based models are all about attention.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=134)** It's about helping the model better understand context so it can generate something that makes sense.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=141)** This attention is not only used for text, but now can increasingly be used for images as well.
>
> **[2:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=147)** It can help image generators find faces or key parts of an image.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=152)** Another interesting innovation has been the rise of what's called self attention.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=157)** That at first might sound like self care.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=159)** You can almost imagine an AI transformer taking a yoga break, but a self-attention transformer can go through terabytes or even petabytes of data and understand the relationship between a word order and the purpose of the sentence.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=175)** It can do this with very little human intervention.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=178)** The system can generate words in a sentence or parts of an image based on a much larger context.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=184)** That means that the system can generate a sentence like, I want to paint the blue wall in front of the house and also generate, I want to paint the wall blue because I don't like the color black.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=196)** The system will successfully generate the second part of the sentence because it understands the first part.
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/transformers?u=76281980&t=202)** It turns out that it's much easier for AI systems to understand human language by paying very close attention.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** self (3), break, (1)
> **CLI Commands:** find (3)
> **Definitions:** means that (2)
> **Analogies:** such as (1), imagine (1)
> **Speakers:** - in (1)


### 13. Ethical and Legal Challenges

> [[#Table of Contents|↑ Back to Table of Contents]]

#### The alignment problem
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=0)** - There's no doubt that artificial intelligence is a highly technical field.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=5)** You've seen that even the earliest forms of AI relied on computers, data, and programming.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=11)** So it makes sense to think that the challenges that you'll run into will also be technical.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=16)** But the truth is much more complicated.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=19)** In fact, some of AI's challenges will lead to deep moral questions.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=24)** You should consider your responsibilities to users and how they align with your organization's values.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=31)** It's not just about asking interesting moral questions.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=34)** It's a key part of working with AI systems.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=38)** The chance of your work being thrown away because of ethical problems is probably far greater than the chance of some technical issue.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=46)** In AI, the main ethical challenges are: value alignment, algorithmic traceability, copyright, and reliability, like generative AI hallucinations.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=60)** The first big challenge is value alignment.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=63)** In many ways, this challenge is probably the most familiar.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=67)** That's because it's the subject of so many science fiction stories.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=72)** It's when the killer robots decide that their biggest threat is humanity, or it's when the AI in "2001: A Space Odyssey" kills the crew to fulfill its mission.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=82)** It's about the system doing what you said, but not what you wanted.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=87)** The alignment problem occurs when you create an AI system to perform a task.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=93)** Then you assume that it will think and reason like a human.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=98)** In a sense, it's when the AI system does what you tell it, but not in a way a human would expect.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=105)** Imagine working for a health insurance company.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=108)** Your team developed an AI system to reduce costs.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=111)** You rewarded the system whenever it found a high-cost customer.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=116)** That AI system would happily cancel all the policies for anybody over the age of 50, since older customers need more healthcare.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=125)** That would certainly lower your costs, but it would also leave some of your longest-paying customers without insurance.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=131)** The system did what you asked, but not what you wanted.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=135)** It worked to maximize its reward without thinking about any of the moral questions.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=142)** Many of the most vocal opponents of artificial intelligence are worried about AI systems gaining some form of consciousness.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=150)** But the reality is that systems are plenty dangerous with just a little bit of competence.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=157)** With a little bit of confidence, an AI system can make a lot of decisions.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=162)** As systems make more decisions, there's a danger that they become misaligned with human values.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=169)** A competent AI system can make a lot of moral decisions before anyone notices.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=175)** In fact, it might be difficult for humans to detect when these systems are doing something that's immoral.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=182)** Most of the time, it's just working towards a reward.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=185)** It'll be up to humans to go back through and make sure that they're aligned with human values.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=191)** This is especially true when the objectives are uncertain.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=195)** To reduce health insurance costs, the AI system needs to recognize the importance of not excluding older customers.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=203)** If it understands these values, then it can apply them to your future objectives.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=208)** That way, you can still give the system power to make decisions, but at the same time, avoid unexpected outcomes.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/the-alignment-problem?u=76281980&t=216)** You don't want your customer or even society to suffer because of a simple misalignment.

#### Decision traceability
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=0)** - You've seen that sometimes AI systems do what you say but not what you want.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=5)** This value alignment can cause a lot of difficulties, especially in complex AI systems, but that's not the only problem you'll run into with machine learning algorithms.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=15)** Sometimes the system will do what you say, but you'll have no idea how it made the decision.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=21)** This challenge is often referred to as decision traceability.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=25)** It's when the steps the system took to arrive at a decision become really difficult for humans to understand.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=33)** Imagine again that you work for a health insurance company.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=36)** Your company created an AI system that would decide which medical procedures should be covered.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=42)** To build the system, your company gathered enormous amounts of data.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=46)** This is a predictive AI system that would look through past medical procedures and find patterns in the best results.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=54)** To be effective, this system would have to look through millions of different medical procedures.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=59)** Then it would have to look at each of the results.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=62)** If a procedure has a low success rate, the AI system wouldn't recommend it for future patients.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=69)** Now, imagine that a patient calls up your health insurance company and asks if their procedure is covered.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=75)** The AI system determines that the procedure's not effective, and so it's not covered for this patient.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=81)** Now, what happens if the patient asks why the procedure isn't covered?
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=85)** How would the representative answer that question?
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=89)** Remember that this predictive AI system made this decision based on enormous amounts of data.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=95)** Then it saw patterns about which procedures had the highest success rate.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=100)** These patterns would be almost impossible for any human to identify.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=106)** In some ways, this AI system is like a black box.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=110)** The customer representative puts in a request and then the system outputs an answer.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=115)** The more complex the system, the more difficult it is for any human to be able to look into that black box.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=123)** There's no way to make sense of all those decisions and data.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=128)** This problem has become so common that some AI researchers have started developing what's called explainable AI or XAI.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=136)** These systems try to do a high-level explanation for the AI decisions, but it can't always interpret what the machine sees.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=144)** Some decisions are simply unexplainable.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=148)** Of course, as these systems become more complex, it becomes much more difficult to explain.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=154)** This is especially true with newer generative AI systems that rely on massive foundation models.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=161)** These systems are so complex that even the people who develop them are uncertain what would happen if you made changes to the underlying foundation model.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=171)** In many ways, decision traceability isn't really solvable.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=175)** Complex AI systems are simply better than humans at finding patterns in enormous datasets.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=181)** Having the system interpret its decision is almost like trying to explain algebra to a cat, and yes, in this example, we're the cats.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=190)** But for many systems, especially in healthcare, humans need to be in the loop.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/decision-traceability?u=76281980&t=195)** When you rely on these systems, it's important that humans can have some idea of the important steps the machine took to make this decision.

> **Analogies:** imagine (2)
> **Env Vars:** xai (1)

#### Copyright challenges
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=0)** - When you ask a chatbot like ChatGPT a question, you'll get a response that sounds human.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=6)** If you ask it to describe a sunset, it will talk about the mix of yellow, orange, pinks, and purple.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=12)** It will even use terms such as breathtaking, serenity and majestic.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=17)** But if you think about it, what's really happening here?
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=20)** You've already seen that companies like OpenAI are using foundation models such as large language models.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=26)** Yet with all this power and data, these foundation models have never actually seen a color.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=32)** These systems don't have lungs, so how can they describe something as breathtaking?
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=37)** Yet that doesn't stop these models from human-splaining colors, sunsets, and feelings.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=44)** That's because generative AI models copy what humans say and make it seem like you're talking to a person.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=51)** It seems like a conversation, but it's just generating sentences from a huge word cloud of probabilities and data.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=59)** But this brings up a key issue.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=61)** If 100,000 humans describe a sunset, do these humans own what they've said or can a large language model vacuum up their words and then use them to start new conversations?
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=73)** Now, most human authors are protected by something called copyright.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=78)** I have some protection for the words that I'm saying right now.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=82)** The reason is pretty straightforward.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=84)** If everyone just copied what I said, it would be harder to control my ideas.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=89)** If this video gets copied and recopied, then it harms the value of the work.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=93)** If you could watch the same video on YouTube or Vimeo, then there's less incentive for you to visit me here.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=101)** Even though copyright protection is broad, there are a few exceptions.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=105)** One of them is called fair use.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=108)** It means that you could freely use copyright material in a way that's still fair to the author.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=114)** Fair use balances the value of the work against the public's need to get new information.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=121)** That means that you can post a link to this video or share a quotation without harming the value of the original work.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=129)** Now, one of the biggest areas of uncertainty is whether large language models fall under this fair use exception.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=137)** Companies like OpenAI say that training their model on the world's data falls under fair use.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=143)** They say it's just like a super intelligent human that goes to every library in the world and reads everything.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=149)** Then they use that knowledge to answer the world's questions.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=153)** While Google trains their model on similar data, its Gemini chatbot often provides a link to the original work.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=160)** Publishers, such as The New York Times, claim that training these models is not fair use.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=165)** When a model summarizes an article, it harms the original value because that person's less likely to buy their newspapers or visit their website.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=175)** This issue may appear as a simple legal disagreement, but it poses significant threat to large language models.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=181)** If most of this material is protected, then that means that these chatbots will lose a lot of their data.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=188)** On the other hand, if it is fair use, that could make it harder for content creators to control their work.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=194)** So many authors might start publishing in places where large language models don't have access.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/copyright-challenges?u=76281980&t=199)** That means that future chatbots could very much hinge on the outcome of this decision.

> **Code Keywords:** protected (2), public (1), super (1)
> **Analogies:** such as (3), just like (1)
> **CLI Commands:** make (2)

#### Privacy concerns
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=0)** - In life, there are rules and then there's guidelines.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=4)** The rules are pretty clear.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=5)** You shouldn't steal or cheat.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=8)** The guidelines are a little bit more flexible.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=10)** Like you should never get a tattoo in a language you don't understand, or you should never eat anything you found in the back of a work fridge.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=18)** In the United States, privacy is just a set of guidelines.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=21)** There isn't the type of hard and fast rules that you see in other countries.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=26)** Many large companies are free to collect your data.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=29)** They can use that data to train their AI models and even sell your data to a third party.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=35)** A lot of what keeps companies from collecting everything is the response that they'd get from their customers.
>
> **[0:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=41)** When people use their smartphone or their credit card, they don't want to have a sense of who owns that data.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=48)** In the United States, the courts have often said that you can't get protection for facts.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=53)** That means that all the contact names in your phone's address book are not protected.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=58)** At first, it might sound strange that your list of friends or your credit card transactions don't belong to you, but courts have often held that this data belongs to whoever collects it.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=69)** If you install an address book app, they can't own your facts, but they can own the database.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=76)** You can almost think of it like a recipe book where they can't own the ingredients, but they can own the cooking, preparation and description.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=84)** They can't own your friends' names, but they can own a database that contains those names.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=91)** They may even include how many times they call and where they call from.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=95)** Privacy protection is about creating a barrier between your personal information and your ability to freely move through society.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=103)** Almost everyone has some expectation of privacy.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=107)** People will usually say things to their friends that they wouldn't say to a stranger.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=111)** Most people act differently at home than they would on a public bus.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=115)** Privacy protection can replicate these barriers through laws and regulation.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=120)** These rules can put restrictions on what companies do with your data, but they can also allow you to request that that data about you is deleted.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=129)** So think about it this way.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=131)** Imagine that you're working on a team that's developing an AI system.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=134)** This system relies on a massive amount of data.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=137)** If you gather a lot of personal information, there are good regulations to follow in the European Union.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=143)** If your customer lives in the United States, then a lot of the privacy guidelines are based on perception.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=150)** These are the general perceptions that your company conveys about how much they care about privacy.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=156)** If customers discover that you collect massive data, then they might develop negative perceptions about your company.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=162)** The company Meta was collecting enormous amount of data about their customers.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=166)** Most of the data capture was legal, but when customers found out, they were less inclined to use their products.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=173)** In a sense, Meta ignored the guidelines.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=177)** If many of your customers are in the United States, it's important to focus more on guidelines.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=182)** Remember, if there's no rule against it, it doesn't mean that it's in your company's best interests.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/privacy-concerns?u=76281980&t=187)** If your company is perceived to be bad on privacy, it could have a real impact on your success.

#### Applying AI to solve problems
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=0)** - In this course, you got an overview of the technology behind artificial intelligence.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=5)** You saw the field started with key concepts, such as the general problem solver and symbolic reasoning.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=11)** Then you saw how machine learning got a slow start, but then quickly became a dominant field in AI.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=16)** You got an overview of machine learning concepts and technology.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=19)** You've seen how several different machine learning algorithms can help learn from massive data sets.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=25)** You also saw how artificial neural networks could be used with machine learning to get deeper insights and find complex patterns.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=33)** Finally, you saw how your network uses back propagation to learn from its mistakes and improve its accuracy.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=39)** I hope that throughout the course you got a sense for how to apply some of these technologies to help solve complex problems.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=46)** You should also think about some of the ethical challenges behind AI.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=50)** Is it okay to have machines make decisions about your health, welfare, and financial credit?
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=56)** These decisions could come from a black box where you have no idea what the machine understood.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=61)** If you're interested in these issues, I've also created a data ethics series, which might be a good follow up to this course.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=67)** As always, please feel free to follow me on LinkedIn.
>
> **[1:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=71)** There you'll see articles and links about artificial intelligence, data ethics, and key business challenges.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-artificial-intelligence-24947908/applying-ai-to-solve-problems?u=76281980&t=77)** Thank you for watching this introduction to artificial intelligence.
